text:
I made this cake yesterday and it turned out very well.  I live on the Mexican border so I have had this cake many times in restaurants and at parties.    I did make a few changes to lesson the calorie and fat content and it still tasted authentic. First I would tell you to read the directions carefully.  The cake has 3 parts ; batter,filling and topping.  The first 6 ingredients make the batter. Be sure to put only one cup of sugar in the batter not 2. The next 3 ingredients make the 3 milk mixture for the filling hence the name three milk cake.  I chose not to use whole milk but used 1% and used only 1 cup along with the other 2 milks.    I made the cake in a 9x13 pan not a round pan as seen in the picture.  The cake was a little flat but that is ok because as you add the 3 milk mixture it expands .  After the cake was done I pierced the cake many times with a fork , all over the cake. You want to make a lot of holes for the milk to saturate the cake.  After you pour the milk on , you want to cover with foil and refrigerate for several hours.  I chose to use cool whip as the topping instead of the whipping cream-sugar mixture.  That cut down on a lot of the calories and was very good.  After I covered the saturated cake with cool whip I covered with foil again and refrigerated for another several hours. You want it to be very cold when you serve it.  I know this has been long but wanted to share my changes and suggestions on making this cake.  Good luck!

text:
I am from Panama and have been making this cake for over 20 years and am constantly making changes to make it even better. This is my favorite cake ever and it is always a hit! A few suggestions:
1 - The toppings can vary from cherries to coconut to cajeta (caramelized milk).
2 - I never use regular milk or whipping cream. Instead I use half & half. I also recommend using either eggnog or coconut milk.
3 - Most of the time, I don't make the cake from scratch - instead I use white cake mix (I don't recommend the butter cake mix for this recipe). When the cake is ready, I cut off the sides and the top to let the cake soak up the milk. 
4 - Always let the cake sit overnight in the fridge...letting the cake soak up the milk makes it even better! Plus this way you can decide whether to take out the milk or leave it in (I like to leave it all in).
5 - Kahlua and Rum adds a great kick to this cake!!! I've even heard of tequila-lime tres leches. 

Basically this is such a versatile recipe with millions of ways to make it your own!

text:
My recipe is nearly identical - except I follow a slightly different method for making the cake portion - beat the butter first, for a few minutes until it is a light yellow color - then add the sugar and beat on high until it is very pale - add eggs one at a time (beating for 20 seconds between each egg); then add vanilla and beat for one more minute.  Add flour mixture a little at a time and mix until batter is smooth (my batter is always a bit thick).  For a slightly better rise in the cake add 1/4 tsp baking soda with the baking powder.  

I like to use 1 cup heavy cream and 1 cup whole milk (essentially half and half) instead of all regular milk... provides a creamier flavor.  

Can be made without the whipped topping if you prefer - it's good with or without it.  

You will NOT be disappointed in this cake - very very delicious!

text:
This is the second recipe that I have tried for Tres Leches, and it came out perfect.  I read all of the previous reviews, and I must disagree with several of the earlier comments.  This cake does not taste eggy (I used 5 large eggs, maybe the other guy used jumbo).  Using a 13x9 pan, the thickness was just right, about 1-1/4" high (cake portion).  There was not too much liquid.  I found the amount of liquid to be almost perfect.  The only problem was having to wait a while for it all to soak in.  I did not want to wait any longer, so I had to dump a few ounces, so I could proceed to the frosting stage.  Once I was serving the cake, I found that it was totally moist, but I would have preferred some excess milk mixture at the bottom, which this one did not produce (the amount missing was just about the amount I threw out), so I think the recipe is probably perfect on quantities and perfect on cooking instructions.  Out of 7 people at my dinner party, 6 loved the cake and one was neutral.

Thank you Stephanie for a great recipe

text:
Overall this is a very good recipe. To ensure you have a good cake, make sure you mix the batter halves exactly.  To get a good rise to the cake, make you you whip the egg whites to merenge-like batter.  Then gently fold in the the flour batter until blended.  Do not overmix or your cake will be flat.  Bake cake until you have a nice brown top where a toohpick comes out clean and cool. (Hint: in a confection oven, I bake this at 325 degrees for 20 minutes.)

As far as the milk mixture goes, I omit the whole milk and just blend together the three milks (hence the name Tres Leches) heavy cream, evaporated milk, and condensed milk together.  After you have punched holes into the made cake, pour half the milk mixture into the cake.  The cake will absorb the mixture.  Refrigerate at least an hour.

When serving, I cut out squares of cake out, not using the cake sides. I place a square cake serving into a small bowl.  I pour milk mixture on top of the cake until it is all the way to the top or half way to the cake.  A small dab of whipped topping and topped with a maraschino cherry and decorate with a tinge of cherry juice over the whipped topping.

By the time you will serve this, the milk mixture will be absorbed into the cake.

For my tough family of food critics, this recipe gets rave reviews!
Thank you for shraing this recipe!

text:
It truly is a great Tres Leches but here are a few very important steps taught to me by a Honduran friends mom. IMPORTANT!! Take the cake out when done to cool, don't touch it, turn off the oven & set the timer for 5 mins. After 5 mins THEN poke the holes in the cake using the large end of a chopstick making larger holes then fork tines, pour the liquid on the top & RETURN to the off oven for 10 mins. The reasons. 1) the cake is still cooking when you take it out so poking holes at that time reseals them, hence no absorption. 2) the dwindling heat slowly forces the liquid into the cake. Also, I substitute a cup of coconut "cream" NOT coconut "milk", for whole milk.
Proceed with the topping when cooled. You will be shocked how unbelievably moist but non soupy this turns out when done this way. Enjoy!!

text:
I love this cake, it was exactly what I wanted.  I grew up eating Tres Leches cake, and the only problem I always had buying them from some stores or bakeries is that they were sickeningly sweet.  This one wasn't like that at all. Now, the only thing different I did was make a different frosting since I hardly ever have cream.  Also, I read mixed reviews on separating the eggs.  I didn't do it and since I liked it as is, I don't have a reason to do more work!  But that's just me.  Also, another reviewer mentioned that the cake is soggy.  YES!  That's how it's supposed to be.  When you sink your fork into it, the milks should ooze out.  It shouldn't be swimming in milk, neither should it be dry.  If you don't like the idea of a wet cake, then I suggest you try a more traditional cake because you may not like this one.  Thanks for posting the recipe!

text:
Wonderful recipe! Very authentic. My husband is Nicaraguan and, yes, as other reviewers have stated, Nicaragua is the origin of the tres leches cake - although other Latin cultures have embraced and modified it. I added a good pinch of nutmeg and about 1/2 tsp of cinnamon to the dry ing. to boost the flavors. For the milk mixture I used 2 full size cans condensed milk, 2-5 oz. cans evaporated milk and 1 c. 2% milk because it was all I had.  It worked perfectly. My cake (9 X 13) did not come out flat and that might be because I allowed quite a bit of whipping time after I added the eggs. I refrigerated the cooled and milk-soaked cake overnight and the next morning added a layer of chopped strawberries and on top of that heavy whipping cream whipped with 1 tsp. good vanilla and about 1/3 c. pwd sugar. In my opinion, the cake would be too sweet with any more sugar than that. Great recipe! I might try it next time with coconut milk (replacing the 2%), rum extract and mangoes.

I have made this cake 3 times.  First time I followed the recipe exactly, then I started tinkering with the method.  Here's what I came up with: (1) not necessary to grease and flour pan (2) not necessary to mix flour and baking powder separately; also not necessary to add it 2 Tbsp at a time - just dump in the flour and baking powder (3) I *did* find it necessary to beat well after each egg addition.  This produced a better textured cake.  THANKS, STEPHANIE, FOR THIS RECIPE!

text:
I have made this cake three times now, and this is what I learned in my own personal test kitchen:
1) I don't bother separating the eggs:  If you beat the egg whites separately (as other reviewers recommend), the remaining batter is so dry (with only the butter and egg yolks for moisture, it is almost like a paste), that at the time of folding in the beaten egg whites, you loose most of the air you have just beaten into them.  I have done it both ways, and saw little to no difference.  I did add ¼ tsp baking soda to help the baking powder raise the cake.
2) More leche please!  For my taste, even  with one can of condensed milk, one of evaporated and 2 of half and half, the cake needed more liquid.  This may depend on personal taste, but for me a tres leches has to be oozing liquid.
3) If you are like me, and once a cake is made you can't stop eating, try half the recipe in an 8x8 pan and half all the ingredients.  The original 5 eggs can be best split as 2 whole and 1 separated egg white.  Leaving out the third yolk, also cuts on the eggy taste (which is not overpowering - the smell in the fresh cake is stronger than the taste in the finished recipe).
4) I used confectioner’s sugar for the whipping cream
5) Don’t hold back on plucking holes: This is what gets the liquid into the cake.  The more the better

I first made this recipe back in 2007 for my friend's birthday. (Infact, my profile picture is this cake haha.) Anyway, I swear by this cake because it truly is delicious. Way better than the Culinary Institute of America's recipe for Tres Leches cake, by the way. 

Here's a few secrets to this cake: #1) Replace AP Flour with Cake Flour and it's a way better product. I've made this cake all sorts of ways, and cake flour is gonna be your best shot for an impressively delicious cake. #2) If you let this cake sit in the fridge for 2 whole days, it is OUT OF THIS WORLD ABSOLUTELY AWESOME. Like, seriously. 2 days is the secret. The texture is crazy amazing.

text:
Results: Cake was very tasty and very moist.  It was completely saturated with the milks.  It was quite sweet, and IMO, went really well with a dark tea.  Making the cake was reasonably easy.  The flavors were quite balanced, and the taste of the milks did come through.

Thoughts on recipe: I used the amount of liquid specified.  At times, I thought there was no chance it would all be absorbed into the cake, but it was. (But barely, and after some time sitting)  Rather than taking the cake out of the pan before putting the milks in, I would recommend adding the milks with the cake in the pan, so that the liquid which falls over the side of the cake while pouring will eventually be absorbed through the bottom of the cake.

If I were to make this again: It's a fairly simple recipe, so I don't think I'd want to tweak too much.  I tend to like cakes which aren't super sweet, so I might consider using a little less sugar in the cake batter itself.  I also wonder if it would be a good twist to add a little extra flavor (nothing TOO strong) to the milks/batter, perhaps a little more vanilla or coconut milk or nutmeg to help the cake be even more aromatic.

text:
This is a solid recipe for Milk Cake - in other words, someone from Mexico will recognize it as Milk Cake.  However, I'd definitely recommend reducing the sugar for the frosting to 1/4-1/2 of a cup (a whole cup of sugar makes a very sweet - too sweet - frosting.  Otherwise, perfect.  Also, add sliced strawberries & bananas to the top of the cake before frosting.  The fruit helps to reduce the overall sweetness of the cake.  I love really sweet cakes & desserts, but if you don't alter this cake slightly it almost feels like you're eating sugar (not quite, but it is that sweet!).

Enjoy!

text:
I made this Saturday morning for a get together on Sat. Night.  My husband is Mexican, and my friends love Tres Leches...so the test was on!  I followed the recipe exactly except for only one thing:  I separated yokes from whites and whipped up whites to a froth before folding them in.  The cake bather was thick, and I had to spread it to the corners of the pan to cover.  After baking, I let it cool and hour before poking holes.  Poured the mixed milks on top, covered, and set in fridge for about 10 hours.  Right before serving, I whipped up the heavy whipping cream, topped cake, added sliced strawberries for effect.

I am not keen on wet cakes, [and that is what tres leches is suppose to be....very, very wet] and so I asked my husband and friends if the cake was too soggy & that maybe I should put in a cup less milk  [the cake had a bit of milk at the bottom, as other reviews described].   My husbands response was, "if you did that, it wouldn't be tres leches, it would be 2 and a half leches"...and then went on to say the cake was perfect!...and friends asked for recipe.

Just so there's no misunderstanding here, I used a boxed white cake mix and cool whip topping instead of the homemade cake and whipped cream the recipe called for.  However, I did use the ingredients for the milk mixture that you pour on top and I followed one of the reviewers suggestion to remove the skin on the top of the cake while its warm to make absorption of the liquid easier.  I also made a fruit topping of blueberries, mango's and strawberries, dressed in honey and lime juice, which I served on the side (not everybody likes fruit).  I know that it almost isn't even the same recipe, but it worked out so well that I wanted to let everyone know that there is an easier, quicker way to make this.  The cake was an absolute HIT at the party I brought it to.  People even went back for seconds!

text:
Awesome!  I used this recipe because I couldn't find mom's.  Now this is my recipe.    I got rave reviews from all the guests including my sister-in-law who asked me to bring it to her Cinco de Mayo party.    This cake is easy to make and quick (1 hr from when I start mixing to when is out of the oven including cleaning up the kitchen).  The second time around I made the following changes and it came better than the first time:     Beat the egg whites and stir them into the mix (sugar, butter, egg yolks) before the flour, then add the flour 1/8 cup at a time.  My Kitchen Aid mixer was on the next to lower speed to do the stir.   With a serrated knife (I used a bread knife), remove the thin layer from the top of the cake before pouring in the milk.  It absorbed the liquid quick and didn't have to sit overnight, only about 6 hrs in the fridge.  I cut the whole milk to one cup (from two because it was all I had in the house).  The milk mixture was a little thicker and the guests loved that.

text:
This cake was absolutely delicious!!!  It was my first time making tres leches and it was so easy!  I did make a few changes based on other reviews.  I used a boxed vanilla cake mix and used a tub of fat free whipped topping instead of making my own whipped cream.  I omitted the the whole milk and instead used a can of coconut milk.  Also I used fat free sweetened condensed milk and fat free evaporated milk.  I had no problems with there being too much liquid, in fact some parts were still dry after it sat in the fridge overnight.  I probably just didn't poke enough holes in the cake.  Finally on top of the whipped topping I added fresh strawberries and canned pineapple chunks.  The pineapple was a fantastic addition, it went perfectly with the coconut milk in the cake!  All in all this tres leches was delicious and my Mexican friends loved it!!  I will definitely make this cake again!!!

text:
Disclaimer: If you do not like ULTRA sweet cakes, this is NOT for you! I had never made Tres Leches, so I was not aware of how intensely sweet it would be. It is a very delicious cake and easy to make, but next time I am absolutely going to cut down on the sugar. I would recommend cutting the sugar for the whipping cream in half because the sweetened condensed milk already gives it enough. I made the cake the night before, poured the milk over it early morning, chilled it covered in the refrigerator all day and a few hours before dinner added the whipped cream, and chilled it again. I used coconut milk instead of regular milk, and added coconut shavings to the top. This added very good flavor.

text:
WOW, JUST INCREDIBLE 10 STARS ********** Made 2 cakes a day ahead ~ COOL WHIP TOPPED. Both less sugar to 3/4 Cup, 1/4 Cup less whole milk, separated the yolks & beat whites, nicely folded in (Alternating) Flour & Whites. (While the cake bakes in oven, put together the sweetened condensed & evaporated & whole milk in Pour-able mixing bowl). Have Fork/Skewer ready when cake is done baking, IMMEDIATELY & QUICKLY poker your cake a lot, the edges & all-throughout. QUICKLY ADD THE MILK MIXTURE to poked cake so that it absorbs easily since it's warm. Let Cool. Then put in fridge until it's Cold. COOL WHIP TOPPED ENTIRELY ~ Put back in the fridge (we love it chilled) until you can Enjoy it!(We have known some folks to leave this cake out to room temp. as well, so whatever your preference)  We loved the 2nd cake too +24 hours later, all the flavors mingled, it was Just So Much More Incredibly Delicious, Enjoy MUCH!!

At first I was dissapointed with this cake, because it seemed bland the first day.  Then the second day it was really good, and today the third day, the cake is the best thing i have ever had.  The key is to let the cake refrigerate a couple days so everything soaks in. Oh- and for anyone making this cake for the first time, the batter is going to be think and i was worried the pan suggested was too big but once you put the whipped topping on and everything it is just right.  And the cake will come out thicker and more dense (it's ment to be that way).  Just add all the liquids and it will be moist by day 2.

I think most of these negative reviews must be from people who have never had a real tres leches cake before. I made the mistake of beating the egg whites like many reviewers suggested and my cake came out light and fluffy (not a tres leches cake). It is supposed to be very dense almost like a corn bread, not light and fluffy. If you follow the recipe you will get a great tres leches cake, not a typical light and fluffy cake.

I made this cake yesterday and refrigerated it overnight.  It is actually better than the bakery cake. This is a wonderful, wonderful and easy cake, and I have been baking at least 50 years.

text:
This cake was an absolute hit with my entire family!  That's saying a lot, too, as they're staunch Mainers who like their "standard" Northeastern US desserts, so a wet cake was really pushing it in my opinion.  Still, they all had seconds and thirds and even asked me for the recipe!  My only modifications when I make this again will be halving the milk syrup mixture as I ended up with a lot of extra pooling in the pan, which made it difficult to transport.  I also used about half of the sugar called for in the whipped cream topping because I prefer my whipped cream unsweetened so I compromised.  The cake was very sweet so I feel it balanced it out.  I tried dusting some baking cocoa over the top of a piece - yummy!  (And can I just say I am shocked that someone would put Cool Whip on top of a cake like this, bleurgh.)  Very simple, very delicious, and definitely something I'll make again for a special occasion.  My son declared it his new favorite food!  :)

text:
I needed a "Latin" dessert for a theme party.  I was very nervous because I've never heard of this cake before...much less eaten it.  I gave it a try based on all the great reviews.  All I can say is UH....MAY......ZING!!!  I will be making this many many more times in the future!  I followed the advice in various reviews by adding 1/2 tsp of baking soda to the cake mix, using 2 cups of 1/2 and 1/2 in place of the milk, pouring the mixture on the cake when it's hot out of the oven, and using Cool Whip on top after it's cooled down instead of real whipping cream (this was just for simplicity - I'm sure the real whipping cream is delicious).  I am in love with this cake!  My new favorite dessert.  Don't be nervous about pouring all the liquid on the cake, it looks like way to much at first but it soaks into the cake like a sponge, right before your eyes. And it's true what everyone says about it being even better the next day.  I just had some with my coffee for breakfast.  Absolutely delicious!  Thank you to the original poster of this recipe.

text:
It turned out tasting better than I had expected. About 150ml of the milk-mixture was left behind after the soaking. It didn't all soak in completely because my cake came out higher in the centre and lower around the edges - hence the milk-mix tended to sit mainly on the lower edges of the cake. To avoid this in future, I'll try making a "hollow" in the centre of the cake dough before placing the tin in the oven. I saved the excess milk-mix in a covered jug in the fridge and served it with each slice of cake. I decorated my cake with chocolate chips (chocolate shavings would be great too) plus 300g of mixed summer berries. They made the cake look lovely, like a sort of "black forest" cake. I also used 1/2 c. sugar instead of 1 c. for the icing/topping. This is a good, easy cake recipe to follow. I didn't bother separating the yolks from the whites and whipping them separately - too time-consuming, and besides, the cake tastes good even if eggs weren't separated before mixing. The amazing thing about this cake is that the longer it sits in the fridge, the better it tastes!! I made this cake for the first time this Easter, and I'll definitely make it again when I have time to bake another cake! Me and my husband finished most of it in 3 days.

text:
This is absolutely the best and easiest recipe for tres leches I have seen.  I too have a few suggestions.  Instead of poking holes in the layers so the milk will be absorbed, I slice off just the very top of the crust.  This allows the milk to be absorbed nore quickly and thoroughly.  I also like to add fruit between the layers and top the whole cake with whipping cream.  Our favorite is pineapple rings with cherries in the centers, though strawberries or peaches work well also.

city:

country:
None
text:
This is one of THE MOST DELICIOUS cakes I have ever baked!!! Thank you for an amazing recipe. It was a big hit at home and work. A few tips from my baking experience... 1) Add 1/4 tsp baking soda to the dry ingredients to help the cake rise really well. 2) When you mix the wet ingredients, add the eggs one at a time and beat well after each one. (I did not need to separate the eggs to get the cake to rise.) 3) Try letting the cake cool in the pan for an hour, then transfer it to a sheet pan. THEN poke holes in it after it's cooled. I used a wooden skewer and poked about 50 holes. Poke all the way to the bottom of the cake. Pour the cream mixture gradually over the cake. When it collects in the sheet pan, drain it into a bowl and start over. Takes a little time, but your cake will be really moist. 4) Let it sit overnight if you have the time. That also makes the cake super moist. 5) Use a little less sugar in the whipped cream if this is kind of rich for you. Fruit on top also adds a nice flavor and cuts the sweetness. TRY THIS RECIPE!!! It's incredible. :)

I made this for the birthday of a friend at work. I found the recipe easy and quick. It got RAVE reviews! I made a few simple changes - I added 1/2 tsp salt; used 1 tsp vanilla in the cake (instead of the 1/2); separated the eggs, whipped the whites and folded them in (based on other reviews); the whole milk I bought was 14 ounces (instead of 16 ounces); and I used 2 cups of whipping cream with 2/3 cup of sugar (plus the vanilla) for the topping. text:
Followed the recipe almost exactly the same but added 1/4 tsp of baking soda to the flour mix to help it rise a little. I used a 9x13 baking pan and it didnt rise so much like a regualr cake but as soon as I added the milk/cream mixture it expanded and I think its a great size. Instead of whole milk I used half & half so it can be creamier. Before I added the milk/cream mixture I took a fork and pierced tons of holes in the cake so the liquid can absorb evenly in the cake. Now with the Whipped frosting don't add 1 cup of sugar, comes out WAY too sweet and I love sweet things. Next time I will add 1/2 cup. I felt like the extremely sweet whipped topping kind of took over the flavor of the tres leche flavor. Coming from a Latin family I have had tons of these in parties and this recipe taste just like those. Great Recipe!

text:
OMG delicious!!  Not difficult to make at all.  I did separate the eggs as other tres leches cakes call for.  I beat the yolks with the sugar/butter mixture; whipped the whites and folded them into the batter.  The cake was not dense at all and created a "sponge" texture.  I still poked holes and took my time pouring the milk mixture over the top-it probably took me close to an hour!  I made it early in the day and by the time we ate it the milk was all soaked in.  I did not top it with whipped cream or meringue- and we didn't miss it.  I was lucky to have real Mexican vanilla which really added to the authentic flavor.  I also added a tsp of vanilla to the topping, as well as a dusting of cinnamon at the end.  I will make "3 Milks" cake very often!!

The basic recipe is wonderful, but for those counting calories here are my modifications:  I made the basic cake recipe as is written, with the slight change that I did separate the eggs as suggested.  For the milk layer, I used 1 can of light coconut milk, 2% evaporated, and fat free sweetened condensed.  I only poured about half to 3/4 of the milk on the cake, and that seemed to be enough.  Moist, without being too rich.  I let the cake set over night and then topped with 1 can of crushed pineapple, covered that with a layer of fat free whipped cream and then sprinkled with strawberries and mandarin oranges.  Was a hit, and everyone appreciated the "lighter" version.

text:
I made this much easier and healthier. Use white cake mix and bake two 9-inch rounds. Poke holes on top of the cooled cakes with a fork. Mix 2 cups of 1% milk, 1can condensed milk, and 1 can 2% evaporated milk. Pour over cakes, cover with foil, and refrigerate. When ready to serve, layer one cake with light Cool Whip, stack on the second cake, and add another layer of cool whip. Throw some fruit on top like strawberries, bleberries, and raspberries. Done.

text:
The taste of the milk sauce was superb. Here are my changes :
1) For convenience, I used a boxed super-moist yellow cake mix. 
2) I added 1/2 tsp cinnamon powder, 1 tsp almond essence and 1/2 tsp orange essence to the milk sauce.
3) I substituted 1 1/2 cups of half and half and 1/2 cup of whole milk for 2 cups of whole milk.
4) I added 2 tbsp of sugar to the milk sauce.
6) I made it the day before.
5) I served it with banana slices and whipped cream.
The end result was amazing - my bf, who is latin, loved it ! However, it is a calorie-dense cake and is heavy on the stomach because of all the milk-fat in it. Tastes much much better the day after, and when eaten cold with whipped cream and fruit. :)

this is a very good recipe. I have a quick and delicious idea for the topping. It is 1 8oz tub of cool whip, 1 pkg of whatever flavor pudding you like (i.e. vainilla, chocolate,lemon), 1 cup milk and 1/4 cup powdered sugar. You mix the pkg of pudding with 1 cup milk and 1/4 cup powder sugar until blended then fold in the whipped topping. GOOOOD and easy!

This recipe is as close to the real thing as one might get. I would like to make a correction for all of your readers.
Tres Leches is a Nicaraguan cake, not Mexican. I give credit where it's due. Mexicans and other Latin American countries may have their own version, but I am Nicaraguan and would like to crear this fact for your readers. 
You might want to also try "Sopa Borracha" a typical Christmas dessert in Nicaragua. 
AM

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
This was not only a first-time recipe for me, but the first time I'd had Tres Leches Cake! I baked it for a party and got raves (not a crumb remained), including from Hispanic colleagues.

I took other reviews seriously, plus added a tweak of my own. As recommended, I beat one (whole) egg at a time, very well. Some claimed that the cake didn't absorb well so wanting to ensure a "thirsty" result, I substituted ¼ c. of WHITE whole wheat flour (very mild in flavor) for a similar amount of AP flour. I thoroughly poked the hot cake immediately to release steam, let it cool COMPLETELY, and poured off the excess milk and re-added it (1X). The very well-done cake had shrunk from the sides of the pan but conformed perfectly soon after the milks (42 oz!) were added (another 1 - 2 oz. of whole milk would've been no problem). The cake rested (covered) in the refrigerator for a good 8 hours before frosting. While I realize TLC is probably meant to be extremely sweet, even halving the called-for amount of the topping's sugar was overkill+. In future: a whole pint (1 ½ c. was skimpy) of cream, no sugar, and perhaps some Dr. Oetker "Whip it" for stabilizing. I also used a high-quality aluminum (Magic Line) 12 (not 13) x 9 x 3" pan for a deeper cake with 3 #7 flower nails, baked for 35 minutes, and HIGHLY recommend Argo baking powder (similar to Bakewell Cream BP).

text:
I read a ton of the reviews for this recipe prior to making it. Lots of good advice, but it started to get very confusing after a while. I read a lot about the "egginess," "sogginess." and "sweetness" of this cake so I altered the recipe accordingly. I used 3 egg whites and 2 whole eggs when making the cake. I used a straw and literally stabbed the cake to death. I halved the whole milk, sweetened condensed milk, and evaporated milk for the milk mixture. I used the Joy of Cooking whipped cream recipe which calls for 1 cup whipping cream, 2Tsp sugar, and 1tsp vanilla extract. I sprinkled cinnamon on top and served the cake chilled at this year's Cinco de Mayo party. It was a hit!

text:
This was the first time I made this cake, my son wanted me to try it so I did. I always read reviews to see what others have done to modify the original recipe.. I did follow one reviewers suggestion on cutting down the sugar and whole milk.. We don’t drink whole milk so I used 1% and only 1 cup of it.
For the topping I didn’t bother with the original recipe… what I did do was use 1- 8oz cream cheese, 1 cup of confectioners’ sugar, 1- 12 oz container of cool whip.. I creamed together the cream cheese and powdered sugar till light and fluffy then I added the thawed out whipped topping and mixed them till I had the thick consistency I wanted.
When I made the holes in the cake I found it easier to use a straw, some of the cake will be inside the straw but I just pushed it out. Once I mixed the “ tres leches”  instead of just pouring it into the holes I filled a bottle with a tip and just inserted the tip into the hole and filled it in.. It was so much faster that way especially since I used a bunt cake pan instead of a 9x13 pan.. 
This recipe is a keeper… Thanks for sharing…………

text:
This first time i ever had tres leches was from this restaurant called Porto's and it was AMAZING and i've been trying to find a way to replicate it ever since. I used Stephanie's recipe mainly as a general guideline. I took some time first to research and read what everyone else thought and gathered that adding just a little bit less than 1/2 a cup of sugar to the batter would help make it not too sweet. Also, using smart balance butter is a great alternative to using butter. You don't notice the difference at all except the tummy ache you usually get afterwards. I also don't like whole milk because it always makes everything too rich so I used vanilla silk soy milk instead along with the condensed milk and i used 2% evaporated milk for the filling and no one noticed the difference either. Everyone loved the cake but to me, it didn't taste authentic enough, just like the slice I had from Porto's. So the second time around I took the advice of using plain white vanilla cake mix for the batter and I used the same vanilla soy milk/condensed milk/2% evaporated milk mixture for the filling and it turned out PERFECT! and also Stephanie should have mentioned it's much much better to make frosting with confectioner's sugar not regular. If you have never made tres leches before make sure to research first! this is a great recipe to use as a guideline but if you want to make sure your tres leches is a hit, definitely use white vanilla cake mix for the batter instead!

text:
To those who think that the cake will become "soupy" or "thin with liquid" are all wrong; clearly those people have never made a tres leches cake before. The cake will be saturated with the liquid and every crumb will absorb that liquid perfectly as you leave the cake to sit for hours. Don't worry, the texture only gets better over time. I guess you can think of it as letting the cake sort of 'marinade.' The longer the better, your patience will be rewarded.

Yummy! This cake is very good and very rich! The only thing I did differently was using fat free or less fat ingredients: fat free sweetened cond. milk & evaporated milk, 1% milk, fat free heavy cream, and wheat flour. Oh, I also seperated the eggs and beat the whites before adding them to the mixture, don't know if that makes a huge difference but that's what I did. The cake had a great consistency, I loved how it was soaked with the milks but it stayed together and didn't fall apart. While the cake was soaking in the milks, I drained the excess milk around the edges into a bowl and re-poured it over the cake so the cake soaked all of the liquid. There was a little liquid underneath the cake but most of it was absorbed. The topping was also very tasty!

text:
Although some of the reviews had me worried, I found this recipe straightforward - with outstanding results. Some small suggested adjustments that can be made, depending on taste:  1) It's a big cake. You can halve the recipe successfully using 2 eggs + a small amount of oil (under a tsp) instead of 2 1/2 eggs.  2) 1 1/2 cups of whip for the topping is generous. You can use 1 or slightly less.  3) The cake is quite sweet, and 3/4 cup of sugar in the base and 1/2 in the topping instead of 1 is fine. I gave the topping some extra kick by adding a generous splash of rum, which my colleagues approved of! 4) To make sure the filling is soaked up evenly - unless you prefer a more varied texture - pierce the cooled base deeply and evenly all over, not just a few times as the recipe suggests.

I tried this because it seemed the easiest of my internet search for Tres Leches. It turned out great. The cake part seemed a bit more yellow and dense than I'd had before so maybe the suggestions below to separate the eggs, etc. might help that, but it was still delicious! I poked lots of holes in the top AND sides of the cake and took the time to pour  the milk in segments to let it all soak in.  At the end there was some liquid that seeped out the bottom which is what it's supposed to do.  As stated before, this cake gets better as it sits in the fridge and chills. It's still good several days later. I added a little Amaretto to the whip cream topping and that really gave it a nice kick! Yummy.

text:
I made this cake for New Years Eve for the first time not knowing how it would come out.  I must say it was delicious and everyone loved it!! the only exception was that I follow a slightly different method for making the cake portion - beat the butter first, for a few minutes until it is a light yellow color - then add the sugar and beat on high until it is very pale - add eggs one at a time (beating for 20 seconds between each egg); then add vanilla (instead of 1/2 teaspoon, I used 1 teaspoon) and beat for one more minute. Add flour mixture a little at a time and mix until batter is smooth. I used almost all the milk ingredients over the cake and it was so moist.  Everyone enjoyed so much that I'm making another one today.

This is a fabulous cake recipe that I made gluten-free.  I just subed GF flour for the wheat flour and added 1 1/2 tsp xanthum gum to the dry flour mix.  Everything else stayed true to the original recipe.  I did pour the milk mixture on the cake while it was still warm and then refrigerated it (without the topping) overnight.  Oh and I reduced the sugar in the whipped topping to 1/4 cup powdered sugar.  1 cup white sugar is way too much.  Sprinkled some cinnamon on top and it was a HUGE hit for my GF daughter and no one else even knew it was gluten-free!

When I went to Peru I had this and was never able to find anything in the states that lived up to it.. till now! This was EXCELLENT! I also used 1 cu. whole milk and 1 cu. heavy cream, I added 1/4 teaspoon baking soda for the cake to rise better, I separated my eggs and beat well the whites before adding, I skipped making the whip cream and used cool whip. I topped with a mixture of sugar and cinnamon. Be sure right when it comes out of the oven to poke holes ALL over the cake and to cut around the edges up the cake. Cake must cool, then slowly pour milk mixture on surface and around the edges. This recipe called for a perfect amount of milk it was GREAT!

text:
I was worried when I baked the cake itself that it didn't seem to be enough cake for the pan.  I also left it in the oven a little too long and it got hard on the edges (completly my fault, not the recipe), so I was worried.  But I poked the holes and poured on the milk mixture anyway.  I only poured on about half and refigerated it overnight, then pour on about another 1/4th the next day after the first has soaked in.  The cake was moist and the "hard" places disappeared.  I frosted as directed and mixed the remaining milk mixture with whipped cream and served it on the side.  The only thing I would change would be to make about 25% more cake next time so it is a little thicker and I will be sure to thoroughly mix in the granulated sugar in the heavy cream before whipping because my whipped cream had some grains of sugar in it still.  Everyone at the party raved about it, though, so I will keep this recipe.

Delicious! I did change a lot in this recipe. I separated the eggs, whipped the whites at the end and folded them in right before pouring the batter into the pan. In the milk mixture I used the condensed milk, the evaporated milk, 2 shots of Malibu rum (coconut rum), and a can of coconut milk. This was amazing and I will definitely make it again.

text:
I made this recipe to use up some leftover sweetened condensed and evaporated milk I had sitting in the fridge.  I only had 4 oz of each, so I reduced the whole milk (which I substituted with heavy whipping cream) to 1/2 cup.  These amounts worked perfectly.  I also followed the suggestion of another reviewer and whipped the egg whites separately, then folded them into the batter.  Finally, 1 1/2 c. of whipping cream was a bit too much for the topping, so I'd only use 1 c. next time.  Overall, this recipe was excellent after a few tweaks.  It has a unique flavor and I'll be making it again!

Easy to follow and so delicious! This one's been a big hit everywhere I've taken it. I never liked tres leches cake before (I hadn't tried it homemade before!) but now it's definitely a staple in my kitchen. text:
I have made this recipe four times as written except I just added canned whipped cream on each piece when I served it.  I read others' concerns about the cake being too dense to absorb all the liquid and made sure to sift the flour and baking powder and that helped a lot.  Also, I softened the unsalted butter on the counter just a little before I whipped it with the sugar and that cut down on some of my prep time - it still took a while to reach "light and fluffy."  I would definitely make this cake a day ahead so it could sit in the fridge and get super cold and the flavors could marry.  The cake as made should still have some liquid in the bottom of the pan.  Thanks for the great recipe!

text:
I have never made a tres leches cake before, but my husband is hispanic and we have had this many times in Mexico. I like food on the dry side, so I don't really care for this cake. But, like a lot of these reviews have said, if you know what this cake is and expect it to be heavy and soggy, then this cake is the best. My husband said that it is almost identical to the one's he's had in the past, and he would know. After reading many of these reviews, I did make one change. I didn't alter the amount of sugar in the cake, but for the milk mixture, I used 2 cans of sw. cond. milk instead of one and decreased the whole milk to 1 cup instead of 2. I poked a ton of little holes in the top of the cooled cake before pouring the milk over, and it took about an hour to soak in. Don't pour any off and make sure you use all of it, or the cake will be dry (at least dry for this type of cake). I hope this helps!

Display Name:
ISCICLES

https://images.media-allrecipes.com/userphotos/50x50/5614259.jpg
city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
It came out perfect! I changed a couple of things.This cake alone is known to be very sweet, but a lil less sugar is better since the sweet condensed milk and the actual cake itself is already sweet to begin with. So I used 1/4 cup of sugar for the whipped cream topping instead of 2 cups and 2 tsp of vanilla extract instead of one. When making the flour mixture, I used one tsp. of vanilla instead of just 1/2. While waiting for the cake to cool off, I mixed the 3 milks and placed them in the fridge to chill. Then, I poked lots of holes throughout the cake before pouring the milks onto it so that way it all settled in nicely. At first I wondered why there was sooo much excess milk liquid, but it soaked it up nicely while leaving the cake overnight in the fridge, some but not all the excess liquid. I would recommend maybe not pouring all of it, but most, the same thing with the whip cream. There will be some left over.  The key to keeping it moist all over is lots of holes! :) In the end, the cake seemed plain-looking, so I added sliced marachino cherries in rows. Afterwards, it looked like a piece of art! And note...the cake is thin at first, but once the milks settle in...it will expand and sponge up. ;) Thanks, Stephanie for the recipe! p.s. this cake is to be served in little portions, due to the sweetness, not the regular size of birthday cake portions.

With a few changes, this recipe turned out really well. At first I didn't think it was going to work, because the batter was very thick when I finished mixing in all the flour, and I had to spread it into the pan rather than pour it. The cake was a little thinner than normal, and much more dense, but I realized that the heavier texture was so it could absorb and hold the milk better.

I followed other reviewers' suggestions and only used 1 cup of milk, rather than the 2 specified. I used skim milk too, and it turned out fine, so whole milk isn't absolutely necessary.

text:
I made it very close to the recipe and I think it is better than our favorite bakery version.  The changes I made were based on a reviewer who had the Honduran grandmother.  I subbed one cup of milk for a can of coconut cream in the milk mix.  I removed the cake after it had finished baking and let it rest for 5 minutes before poking it and soaking it with the milk mixture.   Then I returned it to the oven (turned off) for 15 minutes and it was like magic, the mixture re absorbed up the cake and did not separate even after three days.  We sent half to work and there was still lots for our family.  I also only added a couple of tablespoons of sugar and a couple  of tablespoons of instant vanilla pudding to the whip cream to help stabilize it and it was plenty sweet.

text:
Though this is not my personal go-to cake typically, nor would I say that I will make it regularly, the recipe was simple to follow and worked out great. It tasted delicious for the cake that it is meant to be, and I ate too much of it. Because Tres Leches doesn't typically have butter in the sponge, I decided to beat the egg whites (after separating the eggs) in order to ensure that it's still on the lighter side. I found that I needed to make more than a few pokes with a fork in order to have the filling soak perfectly (I literally made giant gashes throughout the cake since the cake soaks in the filling better and mends the cake in the end anyway). I kept it in the fridge for about 10 minutes to ensure that the consistency was perfect.  My guests loved it and multiple people had seconds.  Consistency was great on day two as well.

I've been using this recipe for a few years now. Recently I thought maybe there was too many eggs in this recipe or maybe I should try separating the eggs. So I decided to go on a tres leche making test for a week and a half. I made 13 different tres leche recipes, including this one in 3 different suggested variations from what was suggested in the reviews. No matter what I did they never turned out as perfect as this exact recipe. They didn't hold the milk right, or were too crumbly, one even had a layer of milk at the bottom that wouldn't absorb for 4 days. I keep coming back to this one. I had to make 4 tonight for a party at work tomorrow and I had to use this recipe. Thank you to the original poster. My family might be a little chunkier because of this recipe but everyone loves it and it never lasts more than a few days in my fridge. I would suggest making this exactly how it's stated. The only difference I use is regular butter and I use confectionery sugar for the whipped topping. Great recipe! A+++

country:

text:
Really good, turned out great! After going through reviews, I used 1 cup of half n half, 1 cup milk, along with the evap milk and sweetened condensed milk.  I mistakenly added the mixed milks after poking my still warm cake.  However, it was fine. Within minutes,all the milk was absorbed, so not a bad way to go. I did refrigerate it for a few hours before icing.  I also reduced the sugar with the whipping cream to a heaping 1/3 cup of confection sugar, along with the tsp of vanilla. I will add sliced strawberries to the top after looking at all the lovely pictures! Thanks for posting this recipe, its a keeper. Can't wait to have a piece with coffee in the morning. UPDATE 10/15-I've made this 3 times and the most helpful things I've discovered: Don't separate the eggs, made no difference. Just be sure and beat eggs well and follow the directions to add the sifted flour spoonfuls at a time.  Pouring the milks onto your poked cake after 30 minutes of cooling (using full milk measurements) will offer a wonderful absorption. Check the cake 25 minutes into baking, mine was done and got too dry when baked for 30.  I made another time when I didn't have enough whipping cream and used powdered cool whip mixed with milk and vanilla for topping and it was great. Hope these things help!

text:
I tried this recipe the first time I wanted to make Tres Leches cake. The cake recipe is just OK for a regular cake. Its missing proper proportions for a moist/fluffy and softer regular cake. 
But the biggest mistake is - Tres Leches cake is a SPONGE cake soaked in three different kinds of milk, and this recipe is NOT a sponge cake. 
Two important things about a SPONGE cake is - No butter (fat), and Separate the eggs. The Egg whites are beaten to stiff peaks, and folded into the batter at the final stage before beating. 
I made the cake again with a Sponge cake recipe (check out Pioneer Woman recipe), and by God! That, my friends, was Tres Leches cake....seriously!

text:
I made this cake for a morning tea at work and it has turned out great. The only suggestions that I would make are too add the milk mixture when the cake is still hot and not to add all of it at once! Keep adding bits at a time, letting them absorb and if you don't need all the milk mixture don't use it. That way the cake turns out delicious and creamy without being soggy.

text:
This cake was so easy to make, no need to leave it overnight. I didn't use milk, I used heavy whipping cream 2 cups, 1 can of condensed milk and one can of evaporated milk. I also cut the sides of the cake and cut the servings in small squares after making the wholes all over the cake, and than poured the 3 milk mix on top and on the sides. The cake absorved the liquid so fast and it stayed moist. For the topping I did not use a whole cup of sugar, I used a little over 1/2 cup and it was perfect! Everybody LOVED it!! Thanks!

text:
I'm a white guy that has never baked anything before (I'm much more useful on the grill), but I decided to make this cake for my Mexican girlfriend's birthday since this is the only kind of cake she likes. I was worried that it wouldn't come out right because I've never baked before, and especially because of some of the reviews saying the ingredient measurements weren't perfect. So imagine my surprise when she said she liked it and it was almost exactly like how she makes her tres leches cakes. Personally I've never eaten this kind of cake so I have nothing to compare it to, but it was interesting. I added self rising flour so the cake wouldn't be so thin, and used a cup and a half of half and half milk instead of two cups of whole milk because I thought it wouldn't absorb that well. But it did, and it left just the slightest amount of milk on the bottom of the pan. It was very moist and not soppy or soaked like other reviewers have said. I poked a ton, and I mean a TON, of holes through the cake and it soaked it up very well. Also, instead of a full cup of sugar for the icing, I used a half cup. It still came out pretty sweet. All in all, a very interesting and tasty cake.

text:
This is a wonderful recipe that is fairly simple and yields excellent results! My husband and his family (who are from Mexico and often serve tres leches cakes at parties) all agreed it was delicious. I made it as stated the first time and it was great, but the second time I used another reviewer's recipe for the whipped topping (1 pint heavy whipping cream, 3 tbsp sugar, and 1 tsp vanilla), and I preferred the latter. Some reviewers have stated that it was super sweet, but tres leches cake, in general, is very sweet. This cake tastes best when made a day or so in advance and not removed from the refrigerator until just before serving. Yum!

text:
**** I made this cake for the first time yesterday.  Having read the directions and most of the reviews, I thought I was "on the way."  However, I must have let the cake cool too much, so, despite all the holes punched, the cake didn't absorb all the milks.  I had to pour some of it off before putting the whipped cream on at serving time. I'm assuming that, had the cake still been hot when the milk layer was added, the milk would have all been absorbed and the cake would have had a softer texture.   The flavors are wonderful, and I'd make this cake again, but not until I hear from someone what my error was.  Although I rated this one at 4 stars, I think it's probably a 5 star with a bit clearer instruction.

I thought that this cake had way to much liquid.  My husband and kids thought the same.  We also thought it was to sweet.  I think the over sweetness came from the whipped cream topping.  1 cup sugar is to much for 1 1/2 cups whipping cream.  The whipped cream did not turn out fluffy like I'm used to seeing when I make whipped cream.  It thickened but it was heavy.  My kids always lick the bowl clean after I make whipped cream in it.  But this whipped cream was so sickenly sweet that they didn't want to lick the bowl this time.  I thought the cake by itself turned out great.  I wouldn't change that part of this recipe.  If I make this again I will make the filling the same but just not pour all of it over the cake.  It tasted good but the cake was to soggy.  For the whipped cream topping I will instead make it with 1 pint whipping cream, 3 tablespoons sugar and 1 teaspoon vanilla.  I've used this whipped cream recipe before for other cakes and it always turns out good.  Just the right amount of sweetness.

text:
A+ recipe! However, I made a few changes. I separated the egg yokes from the egg whites, and added the yokes in just as the directions say to do for the eggs. Then, I added the flour/baking powder mixture 2 tablespoons at a time and beat. I then beat the egg whites separately and poured them into the batter and beat them for about 1 to 2 minutes, then poured them into 2 pans and baked and let cool.

I combined 1/2 cup of each milk, instead of a whole can to prevent the cake from being too soggy, and poured the milk mixture into a medium sized bowl and whisked the 3 milks together. And instead of 2 cups whole milk, I used 1/2 cup of half & half.  

After baking and letting the cakes cool, I poured the milk mixture over them, covered with foil, and let them sit in the fridge overnight.

If you coat your cake with a THIN layer of icing, this should prevent your cool whip from sinking into your cake after you put it on.

Thanks for a great recipe! Will make again and again!

I got nervous & separated the eggs after reading the other reviews. My cake came out perfect. I didn't cool the cake before pouring the liquid over. I let the liquid absorb overnight and iced it the next day. Next time I'll garnish with marachino cherries just for looks. For people who can tolerate a very sweet cake, this is to die for. I think it's the best Tres Leches cake I've ever eaten.

text:
Excellent cake! Tried this once before at a Cuban restaurant and found this to be as delicious. If you are looking for a dry or even moist cake, keep looking. From what I understand, this cake is supposed to be and is WET.  The cake was sweet enough for my taste after the milks were absorbed (1st poked many holes into the cake, poured in 2/3 of the mixed up milks - threw out the rest - and kept it in the refrigerator overnight).  Also, decreased the sugar in the whipped cream significantly as the cake with the milk inside is plenty sweet (in my opinion).  I just made my 1st one and will make another one this week for my husband's Cinco de Mayo work party : ) Thank you for this recipe!!

text:
I've been making this recipe for a long time now, it's my go-to cake recipe. Everyone LOVES it. They say it's better than the tres leches cakes we order from Mexican markets. I follow it exactly, except I don't use the "frosting" they have here. It's not as good. I just use Cool Whip as my frosting. This is delicious and extremely moist. So good. Also, after I pour the milk over the cake, I let it sit for at least 24 hours. The longer the better! After I let it sit, then I frost it.

text:
Excellent, although VERY rich!  Regarding the half and half vs. milk debate:  I measured out my whipping cream for the topping in advance, and then combined what remained from the pint that I had bought with 1% milk for the filling (in addition to the recommended amounts of evaporated and  condensed milk.)  It took several hours of slow and patient soaking for the milk to absorb, and even then there was a little left that wouldn't absorb, but it made a delicious sauce when spooned over each serving.  As a final touch I sprinkled the cake with cinnamon and nutmeg (as shown in the picture).

text:
I had never even heard of this before but my supervisor asked me to make it for a work party. It was very good, I followed it exactly. I had my doubts when pouring on all the milk, I thought it would be too much, but the cake really does absorb it like a sponge and expands quite a bit with the added liquid. There was also a little extra liquid at the bottom of the dish which some opted to spooning this over their slice. The cake was very good, very very sweet and rich and so it serves quite a few people because we cut the slices so thin. The most important thing about this cake is to keep it very cold otherwise it becomes soggy and of course the milk will go bad. Interesting cake, but very delicious.

text:
This was interesting and pretty good.  I decided to bake it on Cinco De Mayo.  I have a tip for other impatient people, like myself.  After the cake cools for about 15 minutes out of the oven, place it in the freezer for 20-30 minutes to cool it all the way before pouring the milk mixture over the top.  Then you need to let it sit in the fridge till the cake soaks up the liquid.  I served with cool whip and strawberries.  It wasn't as popular in my house as most cakes are but it wasn't bad.

text:
We haven't taken a bit yet, but wanted to share what WE did. We took the advice of the Sage One who used Half & Half...and added our own twist. We had double birthdays last month and were surprised by sister, Terry and her hubby Ron, with a wonderful meal topped off by a Spice Cake baked in a round bundt pan. We felt like royalty! Sis is very special to us and therefore WE wanted to do something special for her birthday this month. We baked our Tres Leches in heart shaped bundt pan. German meets Latino! We popped the cooled cake out of the pan then added sliced kiwi and a mixture of frozen berries to the "bottom" of the pan and put the cake back in the way it was baked. We then poked the holes - we suggest a stick of raw spaghetti - poured the milk mixture over all, covered with foil for transport. We've got the fresh whipped cream ready to take along and have great hope that it all pops out properly so we can bring some beautiful AND delicious cake to Terry for her 59th birthday!

text:
Made this for Christmas for my brother who was coming in from San Antonio.  He fashions himself as a connoisseur of fine Tres Leches cakes because it's his favorite.  Huge success!    I suggest that you make sure you let the butter get really soft before mixing it with the sugar.  It's hard to cream butter and sugar if the butter is still clumping up.  I also suggest "basting" the milk mixture while the cake is soaking it up.  That way the center gets it's fair share.

Tasty Tres Leches! If anything I would increase the volume of the milk mixture. I added a 1/4 tsp. of baking soda with the baking powder, added only 3/4 cup sugar with the butter and separated the eggs (mixed the yolks with the creamed sugar mixture and beat the whites until soft peaks formed and added the 1/4 cup sugar, beat until stiff peaks, folded into egg yolk/sugar mix). Served the cake with strawberries and bluberries. Had the cake for desert one night, then brought the remainder to the office. I went to see what was left at the end of the day and found the clean cake pan drying by the sink.

Goodness gracious. I've been looking all over the place for a Tres Leches Cake similar to those I've had while visiting Miami and this one is dead-on! To me, a good Tres Leches cake is dense and soaks up the milk without becoming too soggy. It should also have a rich, buttery, vanilla flavor. This cake succeeds on both points. I didn't even have whipped cream to top the cake, so sprinkled a cup of shredded coconut  top.

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
This is one of the best recipes I have tried for 3 leches - my husband's favorite cake.  I did a few things to make at least a slightly MORE HEALTHY VERSION.  First, I used half Splenda and half normal sugar to go inside the cake (1/2 c. each).  It says to use unsalted butter w/the ingredient list, but in the recipe it mentions margarine.  I just used a lowfat  margarine (smart choice).   (I didn't have any at the time, but you could use egg substitute as well to cut even more fat & calories.) I baked that, and it came out perfect.  For the liquids, I used normal swt cond. milk, but I only used about 8-10 oz of evap milk (you could use low fat, but don't do nonfat evap. milk - there just isn't enough flavor).  Then I used 2% milk to make up the difference until I had a little over four cups of liquid.  If you prick the cake with a fork and pour the liquid in while it is still warm (wait at least 15 min though), it really soaks up the liquid well.  Pour slowly and wait until what you have already poured is soaked in before adding more.  I used lowfat cool whip on top.  Definitely put in the fridge for at least an hour.  To make it just that much more special, when serving I top it with sugared strawberries on top.  Just take sliced, fresh strawberries (or thawed frozen strawberries) and sweeten them to taste.  Again, I use half Splenda and half sugar to cut calories.  Thanks for a wonderful, wonderful cake!

I've never had real Tres Leches before so I have nothing to compare this to, but I thought that this was a pretty good cake.  I followed the recipe as written and used skim milk.  I put the milk over the cake in "layers", but eventually decided to let it sit in the fridge for a while to absorb the milk as it did not seem to be absorbing any more milk after letting it stand for 20 minutes.  Maybe I didn't poke enough holes in the cake(?), but I had at least a half a cup of milk left and a few hours later there was still quite a bit of milk in the dish that had not been absorbed.  It was nice to try it, but I don't think that I will be making it again.

Made this for my boyfriend who is a native of Costa Rica.  He loved it, I was hesitant to try it but ended up enjoying it a lot. Definitely try this recipe if you enjoy tres leches.

I was looking for an alternative to just the usual strawberry shortcake type dessert for summer and found this. This cake is delicious! Regarding another review that said that it was too eggy, I did find it "eggy" tasting when I tried it about an hour after making it. My family has already requested I make it again. Great recipe!

First, I did make a few changes...instead of the condensed milk, I used 1 can of cream of coconut. And I baked in a 9 inch round cake pan. The cake came out much heavier than I expected. The batter was so light and fluffy, I thought the cake would bake up very light too. But the cake was rather dense which is also why I think i had trouble with the cake absorbing all the liquid. I think the cake's texture was just too dense to absorb all the liquid. However, the taste was really good and I had people ask for seconds. I would use this recipe again for a coconut cake...but for tres leches, I want a lighter, fluffier cake recipe.

text:
I loved this recipe and so did my family but I changed a couple things along the way. First I separated the egg yolks and whites, putting the yolks into the batter first and whipping and folding in the whites at the end. Instead of using all whole milk I used 1/2 whole milk and 1/2 cream (aka Half and Half). I let mine sit in the fridge overnight before serving, it’s the best the next day. Also be sure not to add too much vanilla to your whipped cream because it can make the cake seem way too sweet. Strawberries makes a DELICIOUS topping, the cake is pretty sweet so it adds a nice tartness to the recipe :)

text:
I  loved this recipe. Firstly, It was very quick and easy to make and I  added a few minor changes. Second, I  substituted one cup of whole milk for a can of cream of coconut (I  used coco Lopez). I  always prefer this with a coconutty flavor lol.  After reading several helpful ratings, I  cooked the cake I  used a chop stick to make several holes and closely cut off the edges. This allowed the milk to fully saturate the cake which I  did approximately 5-7 minutes after removing from oven. I  then covered with foil and refrigerated for the next day.  it was a huge hit with my sons.

region:
None
country:
None
text:
Moist and delicious!  I made this cake for Thanksgiving and everybody loved it. I decided to make it in a  regular rectangular Pyrex mold and leave it there since I was going to transport it.  Serving it that way was easy too. 
 Once  I took the cake out of the oven I let it rest for about 10 minutes,  then poked the holes with the fork and poured the leche mixture over it. Looking through the glass I noticed the bottom of the cake was not getting the mixture so  I used a thin metal spatula to separate the edges from the glass and the  mixture flowed easily to the bottom.  I also used a bit less sugar both times and it came out just right.

text:
The flavour of this cake was good. It was a little too sweet for me, so I would cut the sugar in the cake to 3/4 cup next time (bearing 8n mind that there is a ton of sugar in the sweetened condensed milk). I find many people like things sweeter than I do so it may be fine for others.  The texture was good, although I took the advice of other reviewers and whipped the egg whites before adding to the batter.

My major complaint about this cake is that the batter is very thick, and spreading it across a 9x13 pan was a challenge. I did my best, but still wound up with an uneven cake, which did not fill the whole pan or soak up the milks evenly. I think the solution is a smaller pan (a 9x9 square, maybe) and longer baking time.  

To serve this, I wound up scooping it like trifle into cups and dolloping whipped cream on top. It was too uneven to serve as it was. It was actually quite a lovely presentation, but definitely not the birthday cake I was hoping for!

text:
This is the best Tres Leches recipe I've found.  I've tried other recipes that begin with a boxed mix, but you can always taste that in the end result.  I followed the cake part of this recipe exactly, and my cake wasn't flat - I recommend really beating the batter thoroughly after each egg and then a minute more once everything's added.  I used Cool Whip on top as others suggested, and I used 2% milk in place of the whole milk/cream.  After a few hours in the refrigerator, all of the milks had soaked in, so I poured more 2% milk over the top (maybe an extra cup).  It all soaked in by morning, and the cake was not soggy at all - it cut nicely into clean pieces without being runny.  Such a solid recipe!

text:
After writing my review of this recipe, I went back to read through a number of the reviews of the recipe done by others and I want to respond to some of those things that have been said and make a few more comments.

First off--I should say that when baking and some cooking--I have a Kitchen Aid stand mixer and I have found that surely for baking----having a mixer unit of this type or made by other companies---is absolutely a must have.

Back in just about every "industrial kitchen" whether a large restaurant, the military or catering services---we had the real deal mixers----big floor model Hobart mixers.  

When it comes to this recipe--I did not separate the egg yolks from the egg whites--I really don't see the need for that--I had whipped my eggs first together using a hand whisk and I did use heavy cream to make my own fresh whipped topping--something I have been doing for a number of years now.  I have not used products like Cool Whip for a long time now because they really are not much that are "real" and mostly chemicals.  

The only preprepared whipping cream I use are the canned ones, they are more "real" than are the ones like Cool Whip.

As to the sugar content of this recipe--it is pretty high and in future runs of the recipe--I think I will both tone it down in the amount of sugar I use and perhaps even the nature of what I use as a sweetner. 

This recipe though--is a good one to tweek to your own tastes and such--and the suggustions that you can add many othe

text:
This cake was amazing!!!  It was the first time I made a Tres Leches cake.  Really wasn't too difficult.  I did separate the eggs, adding the whipped whites to the batter before adding the flour mixture, and used Half and Half instead of the milk, but those were the only changes I made.  Made it 2 days ahead of time, making sure to refrigerate until it was time to eat.  Made the topping the day I was going to serve it.  Sprinkled cinnamon lightly over the whipped topping, then topped each slice with a mint leaf, blackberry, raspberry, and blueberry.  It was so look delicious I actually had another half piece, something I never do.  Eating the mint leaf at the end was a refreshing touch.  Great recipe!

I don't bother with sifting or gradually adding the flour mixture but try to mix it till just incorporated to keep everything fluffy.

text:
Make sure you cream the butter thoroughly until it is fluffy and not just until the sugar in incorporated! Adding in the flour at the very last step ensures a tender cake because if you mix it too much gluten will form from the proteins in the flour and will end up in a dense and chewy cake.

I added in the milk mixture after the cake completely cooled, covered it and refrigerate it overnight (6-8h) to make sure the cake had time to soak in the milk mix completely along with letting it dry a bit so it won't be completely soggy at the bottom.

In the morning I whipped up 2 cups of heavy cream with 3 tbsp of sugar and a dash of vanilla extract, spread 2/3rds onto the cake, put 1/3rd of it into a piping bag with a large open star tip and piped dollops on each serving portion for the berries to sit on.

I adjusted the recipe to have only 1/2 cup of sugar as the condensed milk already adds to the sweetness along with the whipped cream, but honestly you could cut it down to 1/4th as well. I garnished with strawberries and blueberries although you can do whatever you like (peaches, kiwi, blackberries, raspberries, etc etc) and melted some peach preserves in the microwave and brushed it over the fruit to make it glossy for a more professional finish.  This is a perfect cake for the spring and summer.

The version I made isn't sickenly sweet like American Store-bought cakes but more towards asian bakery cakes, but still a tad bit sweeter because of the condensed milk. This will satisf

As others have mention , you do normally make tres leches by dividing the yoke from the whites  and there is a folding together (not just mixing) of the moist mixture with the dry mixture. I have made it that way many times before and it is a little more time consuming and if not done right can come out lumpy however, I was  concerned that this recipe wouldn’t be as good. The only thing I did different was I didn’t add as much sugar to the whipped cream on top. But that’s just a matter of preference. I lived in a Latin American country for 15 years. Some even make a sugary meringue like topping but I prefer real whipped cream with just a bit of sugar.

text:
I made this recipe for my first go with separating the egg whites and folding them in at the end.  The result was a think batter that needed to be spread in the 9 x 13 dish.  

After it came out of the oven, I was skeptical as the product was very lackluster.  It was very dense and didn't rise very much.  None the less, I poked many holes in it with a larger serving fork and let it cool before I added the milk mixture.  The whole dish was then put in the fridge over night.

The next day the cake did not soak up much of the liquid.  I was disappointed and the cake was dry.  So in an effort to save it, I cut it up into squares while still in the dish, while still in the liquid, put it back into the oven at 300F for 30 minutes.

Voila!  It was saved!  It has soaked up A LOT of the liquid and puffed up to look half decent.  I am currently having it cool down to the point where I can put it in the fridge and hopefully by tonight whip up some cream to serve!

UPDATE:  still didn't soak up enough of the liquid.  I think there is a component missing in the recipe.  There isn't enough liquid for the batter.  Many Tres Leches recipes call for some kind of liquid i.e. 1 cup of milk into the cake batter mixed in prior to baking.  Alas, this ended up being a dry brick in the middle....dense, and not very enjoyable.

text:
I prepared this recipe pretty much as is. I must point out that the eggs amount is fine.  I followed a few of the suggestions related to the mixing procedure. The cake came out a bit dense but very good.  I do however have an advice : Try to poke as many wholes as you can so the cake soaks up milk mixture evenly and not partially. The cake might look soaked but you might discover some dry spots inside once you slice it. Follow this recommendation especially if you use a round mold instead of a rectangular one.  A key thing to keep in mind here are to master how to make a good light spongy light cake without resorting to make a meringue. This could be a bit more difficult especially for the novice baker. Practice and get to know the recipe. The other key thing is making a good milk mixture. It makes a big difference.The suggestion of replacing a bit of the whole milk for heavy cream is excellent. It added texture and enhanced the milk mixture. I would recommend to add a pinch of nutmeg to it. I did not do it because I wanted to stick to the recipe as written as much as i could. You will  get a one of a kind flavor boost with the nutmeg still without altering drastically the essence of the recipe. I will make it again! .

text:
Loved this cake but it was waaaay too sweet with too much milk!  I followed the batter portion to a tee and it turned out well.  The same with the 3 milk portion, although I could see it was going to be a lot of liquid, i proceeded since it was my first time.  I bought a carton of heavy cream that had 2 cups and decided to go with that as opposed to the 1 1/2 cups that was required.  I ran out of sugar so only ended up using 3/4 cup.  This was way too sweet, even with the additional cream.  I mean I like sweet stuff, but this went too far!  People said the liked it but no one went for seconds and the host packed it up and made sure I took the leftovers home with me.  Overall I would make it again but  cut the whole milk portion down to 1 cup and cut the sugar in the heavy cream down to 1/4 cup.  I would also add some type of liquor, frangellico, kahlua or amaretto to the milk mix just for fun!

text:
This cake was a hit, but I did make some changes.  First, I added 1/2 tsp baking soda to the flour mixture.  I also used coconut cream (not milk, but the cream that I use to make pina colada's) instead of the whole milk in the recipe.  I also heated the 3 milks on the stovetop until they were all blended together nicely.  Waited 5 minutes after pulling the finished cake out of the oven to poke holes (used a candy thermometer to poke the holes into the cake).  Once the holes were poked, I poured the milks over the cake and p laced back  in the over for 5 minutes (oven was turned off at this point, but was still warm).  The cake has a great flavor - especially after sitting for 2 days in the fridge.  Definitely a keeper!

text:
Mine turned out wonderful!
I added a little more baking powder, added baking soda & not do much sugar in the frosting.   
   
Tres Leches (Milk Cake)

Recipe by: Stephanie"
This cake is made with three layers: Cake, filling, and topping. 
There are 4 types of milk in the filling and topping (whole milk, condensed milk, evaporated milk, and heavy cream). 
This is an excellent cake for milk lovers!”

Ingredients:
Cake Batter
1 1/2 cups all-purpose flour
2 teaspoon baking powder
1/2 tsp baking soda
1/2 teaspoon salt
1/2 cup unsalted butter
1 cup white sugar
5 eggs
1/2 teaspoon vanilla extract (or more)

To pour over the cake after baking:
2 cups whole milk
1 (14 ounce) can sweetened condensed milk
1 (12 fluid ounce) can evaporated milk

Frosting:
1 1/2 cups heavy whipping cream (or full pint)
1/3(ish) cup white sugar
1 teaspoon vanilla extract

Directions
Preheat oven to 350 degrees F (175 degrees C). Grease and flour one 9x13 inch baking pan.
Sift flour and baking powder together and set aside.
Cream butter or margarine and the 1 cup sugar together until fluffy. Add eggs and the 1/2 teaspoon vanilla extract; beat well.
Add the flour mixture to the butter mixture 
2 tablespoons at a time; mix until well blended. Pour batter into prepared pan.
Bake at 350 degrees F (175 degrees C) for 30 minutes. 
Pierce cake several times with a fork. 
Let cool.
Combine the whole milk, condensed milk, and evaporated milk together. Pour over the top of the cooled cake.
Whip whipping cream, the 1/

text:
I have made this recipe many times now (it's my boyfriend's absolute favorite). It is not too heavy, not to light, and has a perfect balance of sweetness. The cake itself is a little dense, but that is okay because the milk will lighten it up. Don't be afraid of adding all the milk. It will all absorb! I've seen comments on it being very eggy, but that is fine because it allows for the right texture, and it also does not taste eggy once the milk has been absorbed.

The few notes I have are: 
I use half and half rather than milk to get the right thickness of the milk mixture.
Beating the egg whites beforehand seem to have no effect on the final product.
Let the cake cool before stabbing it full of holes with a fork. 
Let the cake sit in the milk mixture for 24 hours before icing.
You can use pre-made whipped topping if you would like to.

text:
Ibe made this twice now. My stars rating is for this recipe exactly as it stands. I covered the top the second time round with warm dulce De leche instead of whipped cream. It adds a nice, richer element but whipped cream works well too. I make it a little differently. Seperate the eggs, beat the whites to a soft peak first with a bit of salt. Then add the sugar and beat til firm peaks. Then add the yolks (beaten with a fork beforehand) slowly under the beaters on low speed. 

Then, very gently fold in the other dry ingredients. That's how I was taught to make thie this cake and the way I prefer best. But, as I said - fantastic milk mixture - I've seen recipes that use all kinds of odd combos and this recipe is the best to soak the cake without it turning into a sloppy mess. 

Overall, a fantastic dessert to serve if you want something sweet, light and simple.
