text:
The sponge cake turned out much to dense and bland. The whipped cream was way too sweet. Followed recipe exactly and had to throw out the entire cake as no one could eat it.
UPDATE: After this attempt I was on a mission to find a good, authentic tres leches cake recipe. I live in Arizona and this is my favorite cake. There are many authentic Mexican food restaurants in my area that serve this cake so the bar was set high for finding a recipe that could measure up. I was able to find another recipe o this site for this cake and the difference was remarkable! Comparatively, this recipe calls for copious amounts of sugar, 1 cup for whipping cream is beyond too much. The other recipe I tried called for 1/4 cup and it was perfect at the lower amount. This recipe also calls for 2 cups of milk for the 3 milk mixture, this is way too much. Other recipes call for 1/3 to 1/2 cup of milk and this is the amount you need to not dilute the flavor of the condensed milk. Perhaps the biggest misstep of this recipe is not separating the eggs. Separating and beating the eggs really makes all the difference! Otherwise the sponge is too dense and the texture is completely off.  I decided to update my review after I tried the other recipe for this cake and it turned out so much better. Hopefully the tips in this review help guide those of you wanting to make an authentic tres leches cake.

Awesome cake. Had it before years ago in the little bodegas and was having a total craving for it. Perfect amount of liquid, you just have to wait for it to absorb. You always want a little extra milk at the bottom of the pan and plate. That's how it's supposed to be. And it doesn't taste eggy at all. The batter is supposed to be very thick, if it was too soft a cake to begin with, it would fall apart. Also the cake may look small in the pan, but it's a sponge. By the time the milk is absorbed, it will fill out.  Delicious!

K just made this 2 ways. First off, if you made this just as directed...slap yourself. I had no idea it would make such a difference. I took a picture let me see if I could upload...

text:
This was really yummy and it was a lot like the one I had at a local Cuban restaurant. Everyone liked it!  I followed the recipe, except used half the sugar in the whipped cream. It was still very sweet with the half a cup and a cup would have been too sweet for me. When the cake was done baking it was harder than I thought it would be and I had a difficult time getting the milks to soak in. When I poured them on top they only stayed there a minute and then ended up on the bottom of my pan with the cake floating on top!  I left it overnight but it still seemed like not much had soaked in so I tried to make my holes in the cake bigger and pushed the cake down so the milks came to the top.  Luckily, by the time we ate it later in the day, a lot of it had soaked in (or leaked out of my container, but that's a whole other story.  Be careful!). It was a pretty good consistency, though I might like it more if it sat another night and really soaked it all in. The flavor was great though!  I will make it again. Next time I may take it out of the oven a little sooner than 30 min to see if it's not as hard.

text:
I've been using this recipe for years now and 1) It is super easy to make and  2) always gets rave reviews.

To make sure the liquid gets all soaked in I always try to leave it overnight (in the fridge) to absorb.  Then the next morning I'll put the whipped cream topping in.  Sometimes I substitute whole milk for skim or another variety if I don't have whole, and it always turns out great.  For the whipped cream I cut the sugar down to 1/4 cup or else it is too sweet for my tastes.

text:
This was a good cake and everything turned out as it should but it tasted a bit to "eggy" for me. Next time I would do 4 eggs instead of 5.

Followed the ingredient amounts as listed but did the set up a bit differently. I poked holes in the cake immediately after baking. Used the stem of a regular dinner fork to make the holes so they were big enough to soak up the liquid. Pored the liquid over top of the hot cake, covered with foil and put in fridge overnight. next day milk was totally soaked and iced it with whip topping. Turned out great.

text:
This cake is awesome--I won a dessert contest with it! Obviously the receipe is not for those who are trying to avoid dairy, but it's a wonderful cake for those who are not. I chill the sweetened condensed milk and evaporated milk the night before. I also use the smaller can of evaporated milk, reduce the whole milk to 1 cup, and reserve 1/2 c. of the whipping cream for the milk mixture. You need to keep this dessert refrigerated until right before serving, then make sure you are feeding a bunch of people because this cake does not keep well--leftovers don't work, you have to make sure it gets eaten up when you serve it. I like to garnish the cake with fresh strawberries. For those who might be tempted to take shortcuts and use a store-bought white cake and then pour the milk mixture on it--don't! Make the cake in this receipe, as it's dense enough to soak up all the liquid. Thanks so much for this recipe!

Between the two layers I spread strawberry filling (thinly sliced strawberries, mixed with briefly boiled  water, grenadine, lemon juice, cornstarch, and sugar), which added some extra flavor.

text:
Very tasty! Changes I made were: I beat the eggs by themselves very well before adding them to the batter. Once cooled puncture the cake with a fork to help the milk mixture soak in. Used 2 cups heavy whipping cream instead of whole milk in the milk mixture which makes it a bit thicker. I used cool whip for the topping and squeezed caramel ice cream topping over the coolwhip for a nice presentation. Don't worry, the milk mixture seems like alot, but it is just right.  Once it is poured over the cake refrigerate it and it will almost completely soak in. The only person that didn't like this was my brother who "doesn't like soggy cake" everyone else loves it! Delicious!

text:
This was really good, but the recipe needed a few tweaks.  I used 1 cup 2% milk + 1 cup half-and-half instead of whole milk (was all I had on hand).  The cake didn't rise very much, and I think it might have been because the flour (gluten) was overworked.  Next time I will add all the flour, beating just until blended.  I read the reviews about the cake being too milky, so I added only half the milk.  An hour or two later, the cake had absorbed it all, so I ended up adding the rest (so for next time, I will add all the milk to begin with).  I mixed up a package of fluffy white icing (box mix) for the frosting.  Wonderful!  Served fresh strawberries and blueberries on the side.  Thanks for the recipe!

text:
I halved the sugar in the recipe because condensed milk is already so sweet, and I have a horror of eating too-sweet things...without the whipped cream topping, I think the cake is perfectly sweet. With the topping, it is sugar overload, BUT that's just me. I'd probably use waaay less sugar in the topping next time, or just not use it at all. Other than the sweetness, the cake is superb. I love the moist density and the milky taste. My son had his plain, but for the grownups, I grated Oaxacan chocolate on top and soaked the pieces in a bit of Kahlua. With a coffee or an espresso, it is a coffee-lover's dream. :)

text:
I decreased the sugar, I always decrease the sugar in recipes because they are always too sweet. So, it was roughly 3/4 to 1 cup that I added. Also, the batter was way to thick to pour, it was starting to look more like cookie dough, so I added just a little half and half. For the milk mixture I did one cup of regular coconut milk (using the cream that separates, not the watery stuff, as much as possible) and one cup half and half instead of the two cups whole milk. I also added half a cup of hazelnut kahlua, but next time I would add more because I couldn't taste it at all. And, again, for the topping I decreased the sugar and added a touch of cayenne pepper. It turned out really well, but I wouldcdecrease the milk, because all of it definitely didn't soak in. But, it's  very tasty.

Sorry, but for first time Tres Leches makers, this is not a great recipe.  Too poor information!!  There's no description as to how much time to let the liquid set with the cake.  I gave it 4 hours and the dish was still more of a cake soup than anything else.  I am not an inexperienced dessert-maker, but this recipe did not work out as listed.  Maybe the milks need to be added while the cake is still warm??  Maybe less liquid needs to be added??  Maybe the cake should be allowed to set for 24 hours??  I don't know what the magic cure is, but, as the recipe reads, for first time makers of Tres Leches, I would not select this recipe.

P.S. The actual flavor of this recipe is very good, so if you're not concerned with texture, the recipe, as posted, is just fine.

text:
Super tasty! I baked the cake in a glass pie dish, so it was nice and thick. I also beat the cake batter a long time with the electric mixture, cuz others said they would like the cake more fluffy and less dense. The cake did turn out fluffy and airy. When I poured the milk over I had to pour some on, then wait for it to seep in, then pour more, then wait, etc. so it took a little while to do that. I actually ended up not using about 1/4 cup of the milk, and it turned out great. Just the right amount of moisture. And I didn't add as much sugar to the whipping cream, cuz I don't like it too sweet. I made it the morning of and kept it in the fridge all day, then served it that evening and that seemed to be plenty of time for the milk to seep in and everything to settle. I had never had tres leches cake before, so I really wasn't sure what to expect, but it was really good. And it's a fairly easy cake to make, with ingredients I normally have (just run to the store to get some fresh strawberries). Excellent cake, excellent recipe.

text:
Although this wasn't my favorite cake, I made it for my husband's co-workers and they all loved it!  I made the cakes (4 of them all together) each in disposable pans, they baked up perfectly.  I did pour ALL of the recipe amt of milks over the cakes and it was completely absorbed the next morning.  The whipped cream icing was too sweet for my taste, even after cutting the sugar back to half, so if I were to do this again I'd cut it back even more.  Overall, this recipe was very easy to work with, turned out just like I expected, and was the perfect end to a spicey mexican luncheon!
